If it's None, treat the errors as NON_FIELD_ERRORS.\n\n        The `error` argument can be a single error, a list of errors, or a\n        dictionary that maps field names to lists of errors. An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # Append\n        fields not included in the list in the default order for backward\n        compatibility with subclasses not overriding field_order. Append\n        fields not included in the list in the default order for backward\n        compatibility with subclasses not overriding field_order. If\n        field_order is None, keep all fields in the order defined in the class.\n        Ignore unknown fields in field_order to allow disabling fields in form\n        subclasses without redefining ordering.\n        \"\"\"\n        if field_order is None:\n            return\n        fields = {}\n        for key in field_order:\n            try:\n                fields[key] = self.fields.pop(key)\n            except KeyError:  # ignore unknown fields\n                pass\n        fields.update(self.fields)  # add remaining fields in original order\n        self.fields = fields\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        if self._errors is None:\n            is_valid = \"Unknown\"\n        else:\n            is_valid = self.is_bound and not self._errors\n        return \"<%(cls)s bound=%(bound)s, valid=%(valid)s, fields=(%(fields)s)>\" % {\n            \"cls\": self.__class__.__name__,\n            \"bound\": self.is_bound,\n            \"valid\": is_valid,\n            \"fields\": \";\".join(self.fields),\n        }\n\n    def _bound_items(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield (name, bf) pairs, where bf is a BoundField object.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield name, self[name]\n\n    def __iter__(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield the form's fields as BoundField objects.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield self[name]\n\n    def __getitem__(self, name):\n        \"\"\"Return a BoundField with the given name.\"\"\"\n        try:\n            field = self.fields[name]\n        except KeyError:\n            raise KeyError(\n                \"Key '%s' not found in '%s'. Choices are: %s.\"\n                % (\n                    name,\n                    self.__class__.__name__,\n                    \", \".join(sorted(self.fields)),\n                )\n            )\n        if name not in self._bound_fields_cache:\n            self._bound_fields_cache[name] = field.get_bound_field(self, name)\n        return self._bound_fields_cache[name]\n\n    @property\n    def errors(self):\n        \"\"\"Return an ErrorDict for the data provided for the form.\"\"\"\n        if self._errors is None:\n            self.full_clean()\n        return self._errors\n\n    def is_valid(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if the form has no errors, or False otherwise.\"\"\"\n        return self.is_bound and not self.errors\n\n    def add_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return the field name with a prefix appended, if this Form has a\n        prefix set.\n\n        Subclasses may wish to override.\n        \"\"\"\n        return \"%s-%s\" % (self.prefix, field_name) if self.prefix else field_name\n\n    def add_initial_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"Add an 'initial' prefix for checking dynamic initial values.\"\"\"\n        return \"initial-%s\" % self.add_prefix(field_name)\n\n    def _widget_data_value(self, widget, html_name):\n        # value_from_datadict() gets the data from the data dictionaries.\n        # Each widget type knows how to retrieve its own data, because some\n        # widgets split data over several HTML fields.\n        return widget.value_from_datadict(self.data, self.files, html_name)\n\n    @property\n    def template_name(self):\n        return self.renderer.form_template_name\n\n    def get_context(self):\n        fields = []\n        hidden_fields = []\n        top_errors = self.non_field_errors().copy()\n        for name, bf in self._bound_items():\n            if bf.is_hidden:\n                if bf.errors:\n                    top_errors += [\n                        _(\"(Hidden field %(name)s) %(error)s\")\n                        % {\"name\": name, \"error\": str(e)}\n                        for e in bf.errors\n                    ]\n                hidden_fields.append(bf)\n            else:\n                fields.append((bf, bf.errors))\n        return {\n            \"form\": self,\n            \"fields\": fields,\n            \"hidden_fields\": hidden_fields,\n            \"errors\": top_errors,\n        }\n\n    def non_field_errors(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return an ErrorList of errors that aren't associated with a particular\n        field -- i.e., from Form.clean(). Return an empty ErrorList if there\n        are none.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.errors.get(\n            NON_FIELD_ERRORS,\n            self.error_class(error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer),\n        )\n\n    def add_error(self, field, error):\n        \"\"\"\n        Update the content of `self._errors`.\n\n        The `field` argument is the name of the field to which the errors\n        should be added. If it's None, treat the errors as NON_FIELD_ERRORS.\n\n        The `error` argument can be a single error, a list of errors, or a\n        dictionary that maps field names to lists of errors. An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # Normalize to ValidationError and let its constructor\n            # do the hard work of making sense of the input.\n            error = ValidationError(error)\n\n        if hasattr(error, \"error_dict\"):\n            if field is not None:\n                raise TypeError(\n                    \"The argument `field` must be `None` when the `error` \"\n                    \"argument is a dictionary.\"\n                )\n            else:\n                error = error.error_dict\n        else:\n            error = {field or NON_FIELD_ERRORS: error.error_list}\n\n        for field, error_list in error.items():\n            if field not in self.errors:\n                if field != NON_FIELD_ERRORS and field not in self.fields:\n                    raise ValueError(\n                        \"'%s' has no field named '%s'.\"\n                        % (self.__class__.__name__, field)\n                    )\n                if field == NON_FIELD_ERRORS:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer\n                    )\n                else:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        renderer=self.renderer,\n                        field_id=self[field].auto_id,\n                    )\n            self._errors[field].extend(error_list)\n            if field in self.cleaned_data:\n                del self.cleaned_data[field]\n\n    def has_error(self, field, code=None):\n        return field in self.errors and (\n            code is None\n            or any(error.code == code for error in self.errors.as_data()[field])\n        )\n\n    def full_clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Clean all of self.data and populate self._errors and self.cleaned_data.\n        \"\"\"\n        self._errors = ErrorDict(renderer=self.renderer)\n        if not self.is_bound:  # Stop further processing.\n            return\n        self.cleaned_data = {}\n        # If the form is permitted to be empty, and none of the form data has\n        # changed from the initial data, short circuit any validation.\n        if self.empty_permitted and not self.has_changed():\n            return\n\n        self._clean_fields()\n        self._clean_form()\n        self._clean_composite_validators()\n        self._post_clean()\n\n    def _clean_fields(self):\n        for name, bf in self._bound_items():\n            field = bf.field\n            try:\n                self.cleaned_data[name] = field._clean_bound_field(bf)\n                if hasattr(self, \"clean_%s\" % name):\n                    value = getattr(self, \"clean_%s\" % name)()\n                    self.cleaned_data[name] = value\n            except ValidationError as e:\n                self.add_error(name, e)\n\n    def _clean_form(self):\n        try:\n            cleaned_data = self.clean()\n        except ValidationError as e:\n            self.add_error(None, e)\n        else:\n            if cleaned_data is not None:\n                self.cleaned_data = cleaned_data\n\n    def _post_clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        An internal hook for performing additional cleaning after form cleaning\n        is complete. Used for model validation in model forms.\n        \"\"\"\n        pass\n\n    def clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Hook for doing any extra form-wide cleaning after Field.clean() has\n        been called on every field. Any ValidationError raised by this method\n        will not be associated with a particular field; it will have a\n        special-case association with the field named '__all__'.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.cleaned_data\n\n    def has_changed(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if data differs from initial.\"\"\"\n        return bool(self.changed_data)\n\n    @cached_property\n    def changed_data(self):\n        return [name for name, bf in self._bound_items() if bf._has_changed()]\n\n    @property\n    def media(self):\n        \"\"\"Return all media required to render the widgets on this form.\"\"\"\n        media = Media()\n        for field in self.fields.values():\n            media += field.widget.media\n        return media\n\n    def is_multipart(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return True if the form needs to be multipart-encoded, i.e. it has\n        FileInput, or False otherwise.\n        \"\"\"\n        return any(field.widget.needs_multipart_form for field in self.fields.values())\n\n    def hidden_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of all the BoundField objects that are hidden fields.\n        Useful for manual form layout in templates.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if field.is_hidden]\n\n    def visible_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of BoundField objects that aren't hidden fields.\n        The opposite of the hidden_fields() method.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if not field.is_hidden]\n\n    def get_initial_for_field(self, field, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return initial data for field on form. Use initial data from the form\n        or the field, in that order. Evaluate callable values.\n        \"\"\"\n        value = self.initial.get(field_name, field.initial)\n        if callable(value):\n            value = value()\n        # If this is an auto-generated default date, nix the microseconds\n        # for standardized handling. See #22502.\n        if (\n            isinstance(value, (datetime.datetime, datetime.time))\n            and not field.widget.supports_microseconds\n        ):\n            value = value.replace(microsecond=0)\n        return value\n\n\nclass Form(BaseForm, metaclass=DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass):\n    \"A collection of Fields, plus their associated data.\"\n\n    # This is a separate class from BaseForm in order to abstract the way\n    # self.fields is specified. This class (Form) is the one that does the\n    # fancy metaclass stuff purely for the semantic sugar -- it allows one\n    # to define a form using declarative syntax.\n    # BaseForm itself has no way of designating self.fields.\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":374,"oldLines":6,"newStart":374,"newLines":16,"lines":["             if cleaned_data is not None:","                 self.cleaned_data = cleaned_data"," ","+    def _clean_composite_validators(self):","+        \"\"\"","+        Run all composite field validators for the form.","+        \"\"\"","+        for validator in self.declared_composite_validators.values():","+            try:","+                validator(self)","+            except ValidationError as e:","+                self.add_error(None, e)","+","     def _post_clean(self):","         \"\"\"","         An internal hook for performing additional cleaning after form cleaning"]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

Use a global default if not specified\n        # either as an argument or as self.default_renderer.\n        if renderer is None:\n            if self.default_renderer is None:\n                renderer = get_default_renderer()\n            else:\n                renderer = self.default_renderer\n                if isinstance(self.default_renderer, type):\n                    renderer = renderer()\n        self.renderer = renderer\n\n        self.bound_field_class = (\n            bound_field_class\n            or self.bound_field_class\n            or getattr(self.renderer, \"bound_field_class\", None)\n        )\n\n    def order_fields(self, field_order):\n        \"\"\"\n        Rearrange the fields according to field_order.\n\n        field_order is a list of field names specifying the order. Append\n        fields not included in the list in the default order for backward\n        compatibility with subclasses not overriding field_order. If\n        field_order is None, keep all fields in the order defined in the class.\n        Ignore unknown fields in field_order to allow disabling fields in form\n        subclasses without redefining ordering.\n        \"\"\"\n        if field_order is None:\n            return\n        fields = {}\n        for key in field_order:\n            try:\n                fields[key] = self.fields.pop(key)\n            except KeyError:  # ignore unknown fields\n                pass\n        fields.update(self.fields)  # add remaining fields in original order\n        self.fields = fields\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        if self._errors is None:\n            is_valid = \"Unknown\"\n        else:\n            is_valid = self.is_bound and not self._errors\n        return \"<%(cls)s bound=%(bound)s, valid=%(valid)s, fields=(%(fields)s)>\" % {\n            \"cls\": self.__class__.__name__,\n            \"bound\": self.is_bound,\n            \"valid\": is_valid,\n            \"fields\": \";\".join(self.fields),\n        }\n\n    def _bound_items(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield (name, bf) pairs, where bf is a BoundField object.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield name, self[name]\n\n    def __iter__(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield the form's fields as BoundField objects.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield self[name]\n\n    def __getitem__(self, name):\n        \"\"\"Return a BoundField with the given name.\"\"\"\n        try:\n            field = self.fields[name]\n        except KeyError:\n            raise KeyError(\n                \"Key '%s' not found in '%s'. Choices are: %s.\"\n                % (\n                    name,\n                    self.__class__.__name__,\n                    \", \".join(sorted(self.fields)),\n                )\n            )\n        if name not in self._bound_fields_cache:\n            self._bound_fields_cache[name] = field.get_bound_field(self, name)\n        return self._bound_fields_cache[name]\n\n    @property\n    def errors(self):\n        \"\"\"Return an ErrorDict for the data provided for the form.\"\"\"\n        if self._errors is None:\n            self.full_clean()\n        return self._errors\n\n    def is_valid(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if the form has no errors, or False otherwise.\"\"\"\n        return self.is_bound and not self.errors\n\n    def add_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return the field name with a prefix appended, if this Form has a\n        prefix set.\n\n        Subclasses may wish to override.\n        \"\"\"\n        return \"%s-%s\" % (self.prefix, field_name) if self.prefix else field_name\n\n    def add_initial_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"Add an 'initial' prefix for checking dynamic initial values.\"\"\"\n        return \"initial-%s\" % self.add_prefix(field_name)\n\n    def _widget_data_value(self, widget, html_name):\n        # value_from_datadict() gets the data from the data dictionaries.\n        # Each widget type knows how to retrieve its own data, because some\n        # widgets split data over several HTML fields.\n        return widget.value_from_datadict(self.data, self.files, html_name)\n\n    @property\n    def template_name(self):\n        return self.renderer.form_template_name\n\n    def get_context(self):\n        fields = []\n        hidden_fields = []\n        top_errors = self.non_field_errors().copy()\n        for name, bf in self._bound_items():\n            if bf.is_hidden:\n                if bf.errors:\n                    top_errors += [\n                        _(\"(Hidden field %(name)s) %(error)s\")\n                        % {\"name\": name, \"error\": str(e)}\n                        for e in bf.errors\n                    ]\n                hidden_fields.append(bf)\n            else:\n                fields.append((bf, bf.errors))\n        return {\n            \"form\": self,\n            \"fields\": fields,\n            \"hidden_fields\": hidden_fields,\n            \"errors\": top_errors,\n        }\n\n    def non_field_errors(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return an ErrorList of errors that aren't associated with a particular\n        field -- i.e., from Form.clean(). Return an empty ErrorList if there\n        are none.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.errors.get(\n            NON_FIELD_ERRORS,\n            self.error_class(error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer),\n        )\n\n    def add_error(self, field, error):\n        \"\"\"\n        Update the content of `self._errors`.\n\n        The `field` argument is the name of the field to which the errors\n        should be added. If it's None, treat the errors as NON_FIELD_ERRORS.\n\n        The `error` argument can be a single error, a list of errors, or a\n        dictionary that maps field names to lists of errors. An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # Normalize to ValidationError and let its constructor\n            # do the hard work of making sense of the input.\n            error = ValidationError(error)\n\n        if hasattr(error, \"error_dict\"):\n            if field is not None:\n                raise TypeError(\n                    \"The argument `field` must be `None` when the `error` \"\n                    \"argument is a dictionary.\"\n                )\n            else:\n                error = error.error_dict\n        else:\n            error = {field or NON_FIELD_ERRORS: error.error_list}\n\n        for field, error_list in error.items():\n            if field not in self.errors:\n                if field != NON_FIELD_ERRORS and field not in self.fields:\n                    raise ValueError(\n                        \"'%s' has no field named '%s'.\"\n                        % (self.__class__.__name__, field)\n                    )\n                if field == NON_FIELD_ERRORS:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer\n                    )\n                else:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        renderer=self.renderer,\n                        field_id=self[field].auto_id,\n                    )\n            self._errors[field].extend(error_list)\n            if field in self.cleaned_data:\n                del self.cleaned_data[field]\n\n    def has_error(self, field, code=None):\n        return field in self.errors and (\n            code is None\n            or any(error.code == code for error in self.errors.as_data()[field])\n        )\n\n    def full_clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Clean all of self.data and populate self._errors and self.cleaned_data.\n        \"\"\"\n        self._errors = ErrorDict(renderer=self.renderer)\n        if not self.is_bound:  # Stop further processing.\n            return\n        self.cleaned_data = {}\n        # If the form is permitted to be empty, and none of the form data has\n        # changed from the initial data, short circuit any validation.\n        if self.empty_permitted and not self.has_changed():\n            return\n\n        self._clean_fields()\n        self._clean_form()\n        self._clean_composite_validators()\n        self._post_clean()\n\n    def _clean_fields(self):\n        for name, bf in self._bound_items():\n            field = bf.field\n            try:\n                self.cleaned_data[name] = field._clean_bound_field(bf)\n                if hasattr(self, \"clean_%s\" % name):\n                    value = getattr(self, \"clean_%s\" % name)()\n                    self.cleaned_data[name] = value\n            except ValidationError as e:\n                self.add_error(name, e)\n\n    def _clean_form(self):\n        try:\n            cleaned_data = self.clean()\n        except ValidationError as e:\n            self.add_error(None, e)\n        else:\n            if cleaned_data is not None:\n                self.cleaned_data = cleaned_data\n\n    def _clean_composite_validators(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Run all composite field validators for the form.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not hasattr(self, 'declared_composite_validators'):\n            return\n        for validator in self.declared_composite_validators.values():\n            try:\n                validator(self)\n            except ValidationError as e:\n                self.add_error(None, e)\n\n    def _post_clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        An internal hook for performing additional cleaning after form cleaning\n        is complete. Used for model validation in model forms.\n        \"\"\"\n        pass\n\n    def clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Hook for doing any extra form-wide cleaning after Field.clean() has\n        been called on every field. Any ValidationError raised by this method\n        will not be associated with a particular field; it will have a\n        special-case association with the field named '__all__'.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.cleaned_data\n\n    def has_changed(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if data differs from initial.\"\"\"\n        return bool(self.changed_data)\n\n    @cached_property\n    def changed_data(self):\n        return [name for name, bf in self._bound_items() if bf._has_changed()]\n\n    @property\n    def media(self):\n        \"\"\"Return all media required to render the widgets on this form.\"\"\"\n        media = Media()\n        for field in self.fields.values():\n            media += field.widget.media\n        return media\n\n    def is_multipart(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return True if the form needs to be multipart-encoded, i.e. it has\n        FileInput, or False otherwise.\n        \"\"\"\n        return any(field.widget.needs_multipart_form for field in self.fields.values())\n\n    def hidden_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of all the BoundField objects that are hidden fields.\n        Useful for manual form layout in templates.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if field.is_hidden]\n\n    def visible_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of BoundField objects that aren't hidden fields.\n        The opposite of the hidden_fields() method.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if not field.is_hidden]\n\n    def get_initial_for_field(self, field, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return initial data for field on form. Use initial data from the form\n        or the field, in that order. Evaluate callable values.\n        \"\"\"\n        value = self.initial.get(field_name, field.initial)\n        if callable(value):\n            value = value()\n        # If this is an auto-generated default date, nix the microseconds\n        # for standardized handling. See #22502.\n        if (\n            isinstance(value, (datetime.datetime, datetime.time))\n            and not field.widget.supports_microseconds\n        ):\n            value = value.replace(microsecond=0)\n        return value\n\n\nclass Form(BaseForm, metaclass=DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass):\n    \"A collection of Fields, plus their associated data.\"\n\n    # This is a separate class from BaseForm in order to abstract the way\n    # self.fields is specified. Collect fields from current class and remove them from attrs.\n        attrs[\"declared_fields\"] = {\n            key: attrs.pop(key)\n            for key, value in list(attrs.items())\n            if isinstance(value, Field)\n        }\n\n        # Collect composite field validators from current class and remove them from attrs.\n        attrs[\"declared_composite_validators\"] = {\n            key: attrs.pop(key)\n            for key, value in list(attrs.items())\n            if isinstance(value, CompositeFieldValidator)\n        }\n\n        new_class = super().__new__(mcs, name, bases, attrs)\n\n        # Collect composite validators from base class.\n            if hasattr(base, \"declared_composite_validators\"):\n                declared_composite_validators.update(base.declared_composite_validators)\n\n            # Field shadowing.\n            for attr, value in base.__dict__.items():\n                if value is None and attr in declared_fields:\n                    declared_fields.pop(attr)\n\n        new_class.base_fields = declared_fields\n        new_class.declared_fields = declared_fields\n        new_class.base_composite_validators = declared_composite_validators\n        new_class.declared_composite_validators = declared_composite_validators\n\n        return new_class\n\n\nclass BaseForm(RenderableFormMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    The main implementation of all the Form logic. Note that this class is\n    different than Form. See the comments by the Form class for more info. Any\n    improvements to the form API should be made to this class, not to the Form\n    class.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    default_renderer = None\n    field_order = None\n    prefix = None\n    use_required_attribute = True\n\n    template_name_div = \"django/forms/div.html\"\n    template_name_p = \"django/forms/p.html\"\n    template_name_table = \"django/forms/table.html\"\n    template_name_ul = \"django/forms/ul.html\"\n    template_name_label = \"django/forms/label.html\"\n\n    bound_field_class = None\n    declared_composite_validators = {}\n\n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        data=None,\n        files=None,\n        auto_id=\"id_%s\",\n        prefix=None,\n        initial=None,\n        error_class=ErrorList,\n        label_suffix=None,\n        empty_permitted=False,\n        field_order=None,\n        use_required_attribute=None,\n        renderer=None,\n        bound_field_class=None,\n    ):\n        self.is_bound = data is not None or files is not None\n        self.data = MultiValueDict() if data is None else data\n        self.files = MultiValueDict() if files is None else files\n        self.auto_id = auto_id\n        if prefix is not None:\n            self.prefix = prefix\n        self.initial = initial or {}\n        self.error_class = error_class\n        # Translators: This is the default suffix added to form field labels\n        self.label_suffix = label_suffix if label_suffix is not None else _(\":\")\n        self.empty_permitted = empty_permitted\n        self._errors = None  # Stores the errors after clean() has been called.\n\n        # The base_fields class attribute is the *class-wide* definition of\n        # fields. Because a particular *instance* of the class might want to\n        # alter self.fields, we create self.fields here by copying base_fields.\n        # Instances should always modify self.fields; they should not modify\n        # self.base_fields.\n        self.fields = copy.deepcopy(self.base_fields)\n        self._bound_fields_cache = {}\n        self.order_fields(self.field_order if field_order is None else field_order)\n\n        if use_required_attribute is not None:\n            self.use_required_attribute = use_required_attribute\n\n        if self.empty_permitted and self.use_required_attribute:\n            raise ValueError(\n                \"The empty_permitted and use_required_attribute arguments may \"\n                \"not both be True.\"\n            )\n\n        # Initialize form renderer. Use a global default if not specified\n        # either as an argument or as self.default_renderer.\n        if renderer is None:\n            if self.default_renderer is None:\n                renderer = get_default_renderer()\n            else:\n                renderer = self.default_renderer\n                if isinstance(self.default_renderer, type):\n                    renderer = renderer()\n        self.renderer = renderer\n\n        self.bound_field_class = (\n            bound_field_class\n            or self.bound_field_class\n            or getattr(self.renderer, \"bound_field_class\", None)\n        )\n\n    def order_fields(self, field_order):\n        \"\"\"\n        Rearrange the fields according to field_order.\n\n        field_order is a list of field names specifying the order. Append\n        fields not included in the list in the default order for backward\n        compatibility with subclasses not overriding field_order. If\n        field_order is None, keep all fields in the order defined in the class.\n        Ignore unknown fields in field_order to allow disabling fields in form\n        subclasses without redefining ordering.\n        \"\"\"\n        if field_order is None:\n            return\n        fields = {}\n        for key in field_order:\n            try:\n                fields[key] = self.fields.pop(key)\n            except KeyError:  # ignore unknown fields\n                pass\n        fields.update(self.fields)  # add remaining fields in original order\n        self.fields = fields\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        if self._errors is None:\n            is_valid = \"Unknown\"\n        else:\n            is_valid = self.is_bound and not self._errors\n        return \"<%(cls)s bound=%(bound)s, valid=%(valid)s, fields=(%(fields)s)>\" % {\n            \"cls\": self.__class__.__name__,\n            \"bound\": self.is_bound,\n            \"valid\": is_valid,\n            \"fields\": \";\".join(self.fields),\n        }\n\n    def _bound_items(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield (name, bf) pairs, where bf is a BoundField object.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield name, self[name]\n\n    def __iter__(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield the form's fields as BoundField objects.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield self[name]\n\n    def __getitem__(self, name):\n        \"\"\"Return a BoundField with the given name.\"\"\"\n        try:\n            field = self.fields[name]\n        except KeyError:\n            raise KeyError(\n                \"Key '%s' not found in '%s'. Choices are: %s.\"\n                % (\n                    name,\n                    self.__class__.__name__,\n                    \", \".join(sorted(self.fields)),\n                )\n            )\n        if name not in self._bound_fields_cache:\n            self._bound_fields_cache[name] = field.get_bound_field(self, name)\n        return self._bound_fields_cache[name]\n\n    @property\n    def errors(self):\n        \"\"\"Return an ErrorDict for the data provided for the form.\"\"\"\n        if self._errors is None:\n            self.full_clean()\n        return self._errors\n\n    def is_valid(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if the form has no errors, or False otherwise.\"\"\"\n        return self.is_bound and not self.errors\n\n    def add_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return the field name with a prefix appended, if this Form has a\n        prefix set.\n\n        Subclasses may wish to override.\n        \"\"\"\n        return \"%s-%s\" % (self.prefix, field_name) if self.prefix else field_name\n\n    def add_initial_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"Add an 'initial' prefix for checking dynamic initial values.\"\"\"\n        return \"initial-%s\" % self.add_prefix(field_name)\n\n    def _widget_data_value(self, widget, html_name):\n        # value_from_datadict() gets the data from the data dictionaries.\n        # Each widget type knows how to retrieve its own data, because some\n        # widgets split data over several HTML fields.\n        return widget.value_from_datadict(self.data, self.files, html_name)\n\n    @property\n    def template_name(self):\n        return self.renderer.form_template_name\n\n    def get_context(self):\n        fields = []\n        hidden_fields = []\n        top_errors = self.non_field_errors().copy()\n        for name, bf in self._bound_items():\n            if bf.is_hidden:\n                if bf.errors:\n                    top_errors += [\n                        _(\"(Hidden field %(name)s) %(error)s\")\n                        % {\"name\": name, \"error\": str(e)}\n                        for e in bf.errors\n                    ]\n                hidden_fields.append(bf)\n            else:\n                fields.append((bf, bf.errors))\n        return {\n            \"form\": self,\n            \"fields\": fields,\n            \"hidden_fields\": hidden_fields,\n            \"errors\": top_errors,\n        }\n\n    def non_field_errors(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return an ErrorList of errors that aren't associated with a particular\n        field -- i.e., from Form.clean(). Return an empty ErrorList if there\n        are none.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.errors.get(\n            NON_FIELD_ERRORS,\n            self.error_class(error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer),\n        )\n\n    def add_error(self, field, error):\n        \"\"\"\n        Update the content of `self._errors`.\n\n        The `field` argument is the name of the field to which the errors\n        should be added. If it's None, treat the errors as NON_FIELD_ERRORS.\n\n        The `error` argument can be a single error, a list of errors, or a\n        dictionary that maps field names to lists of errors. An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # Normalize to ValidationError and let its constructor\n            # do the hard work of making sense of the input.\n            error = ValidationError(error)\n\n        if hasattr(error, \"error_dict\"):\n            if field is not None:\n                raise TypeError(\n                    \"The argument `field` must be `None` when the `error` \"\n                    \"argument is a dictionary.\"\n                )\n            else:\n                error = error.error_dict\n        else:\n            error = {field or NON_FIELD_ERRORS: error.error_list}\n\n        for field, error_list in error.items():\n            if field not in self.errors:\n                if field != NON_FIELD_ERRORS and field not in self.fields:\n                    raise ValueError(\n                        \"'%s' has no field named '%s'.\"\n                        % (self.__class__.__name__, field)\n                    )\n                if field == NON_FIELD_ERRORS:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer\n                    )\n                else:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        renderer=self.renderer,\n                        field_id=self[field].auto_id,\n                    )\n            self._errors[field].extend(error_list)\n            if field in self.cleaned_data:\n                del self.cleaned_data[field]\n\n    def has_error(self, field, code=None):\n        return field in self.errors and (\n            code is None\n            or any(error.code == code for error in self.errors.as_data()[field])\n        )\n\n    def full_clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Clean all of self.data and populate self._errors and self.cleaned_data.\n        \"\"\"\n        self._errors = ErrorDict(renderer=self.renderer)\n        if not self.is_bound:  # Stop further processing.\n            return\n        self.cleaned_data = {}\n        # If the form is permitted to be empty, and none of the form data has\n        # changed from the initial data, short circuit any validation.\n        if self.empty_permitted and not self.has_changed():\n            return\n\n        self._clean_fields()\n        self._clean_form()\n        self._clean_composite_validators()\n        self._post_clean()\n\n    def _clean_fields(self):\n        for name, bf in self._bound_items():\n            field = bf.field\n            try:\n                self.cleaned_data[name] = field._clean_bound_field(bf)\n                if hasattr(self, \"clean_%s\" % name):\n                    value = getattr(self, \"clean_%s\" % name)()\n                    self.cleaned_data[name] = value\n            except ValidationError as e:\n                self.add_error(name, e)\n\n    def _clean_form(self):\n        try:\n            cleaned_data = self.clean()\n        except ValidationError as e:\n            self.add_error(None, e)\n        else:\n            if cleaned_data is not None:\n                self.cleaned_data = cleaned_data\n\n    def _clean_composite_validators(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Run all composite field validators for the form.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not hasattr(self, 'declared_composite_validators'):\n            return\n        for validator in self.declared_composite_validators.values():\n            try:\n                validator(self)\n            except ValidationError as e:\n                self.add_error(None, e)\n\n    def _post_clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        An internal hook for performing additional cleaning after form cleaning\n        is complete. Used for model validation in model forms.\n        \"\"\"\n        pass\n\n    def clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Hook for doing any extra form-wide cleaning after Field.clean() has\n        been called on every field. Any ValidationError raised by this method\n        will not be associated with a particular field; it will have a\n        special-case association with the field named '__all__'.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.cleaned_data\n\n    def has_changed(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if data differs from initial.\"\"\"\n        return bool(self.changed_data)\n\n    @cached_property\n    def changed_data(self):\n        return [name for name, bf in self._bound_items() if bf._has_changed()]\n\n    @property\n    def media(self):\n        \"\"\"Return all media required to render the widgets on this form.\"\"\"\n        media = Media()\n        for field in self.fields.values():\n            media += field.widget.media\n        return media\n\n    def is_multipart(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return True if the form needs to be multipart-encoded, i.e. it has\n        FileInput, or False otherwise.\n        \"\"\"\n        return any(field.widget.needs_multipart_form for field in self.fields.values())\n\n    def hidden_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of all the BoundField objects that are hidden fields.\n        Useful for manual form layout in templates.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if field.is_hidden]\n\n    def visible_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of BoundField objects that aren't hidden fields.\n        The opposite of the hidden_fields() method.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if not field.is_hidden]\n\n    def get_initial_for_field(self, field, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return initial data for field on form. Use initial data from the form\n        or the field, in that order. Evaluate callable values.\n        \"\"\"\n        value = self.initial.get(field_name, field.initial)\n        if callable(value):\n            value = value()\n        # If this is an auto-generated default date, nix the microseconds\n        # for standardized handling. CompositeFieldValidator Implementation Summary\n\n## Overview\nI have successfully implemented the `CompositeFieldValidator` class for Django forms, enabling developers to validate relationships between multiple form fields with a clean, declarative syntax.\n\n## Files Created/Modified\n\n### 1. **django/forms/validators.py** (NEW)\n- Created a new module for form validators\n- Implemented `CompositeFieldValidator` class with the following features:\n  - Accepts a validation function, list of field names, and optional error message\n  - Decorated with `@deconstructible` for Django migrations\n  - Implements `__call__` to validate form instances\n  - Validates that all referenced fields exist\n  - Only runs validation when all referenced fields are in cleaned_data\n  - Properly handles and re-raises ValidationError\n  - Includes `__eq__` and `__repr__` methods for debugging\n\n### 2. **django/forms/forms.py** (MODIFIED)\n- **Import**: Added import for `CompositeFieldValidator`\n- **DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass**: Extended to collect `CompositeFieldValidator` instances\n  - Similar to how it collects `Field` instances\n  - Creates `declared_composite_validators` and `base_composite_validators` attributes\n  - Supports inheritance of validators across form class hierarchies\n- **BaseForm**:\n  - Added class attributes: `base_fields`, `base_composite_validators`, `declared_composite_validators`\n  - Added `_clean_composite_validators()` method to run validators during form cleaning\n  - Integrated into `full_clean()` validation pipeline after `_clean_form()` and before `_post_clean()`\n\n### 3. **django/forms/__init__.py** (MODIFIED)\n- Added import of validators module to expose `CompositeFieldValidator` publicly\n- Exports via `from django.forms.validators import *`\n\n## How It Works\n\n### Form Validation Pipeline\nThe composite validators are integrated into Django's form validation pipeline:\n1. `full_clean()` is called\n2. `_clean_fields()` - cleans individual fields\n3. `_clean_form()` - calls the form's `clean()` method\n4. **`_clean_composite_validators()`** - runs composite field validators (NEW)\n5. `_post_clean()` - hook for additional cleaning (used by ModelForm)\n\n### Usage Example\n\n```python\nfrom django import forms\nfrom django.forms import CompositeFieldValidator\nfrom django.core.exceptions import ValidationError\n\nclass RegistrationForm(forms.Form):\n    email = forms.EmailField()\n    email_confirm = forms.EmailField()\n    start_date = forms.DateField()\n    end_date = forms.DateField()\n    password = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n    password_confirm = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n\n    # Define validation functions\n    def validate_emails_match(cleaned_data):\n        if cleaned_data.get('email') != cleaned_data.get('email_confirm'):\n            raise ValidationError(\"Email addresses must match\")\n\n    def validate_date_range(cleaned_data):\n        start = cleaned_data.get('start_date')\n        end = cleaned_data.get('end_date')\n        if start and end and end <= start:\n            raise ValidationError(\"End date must be after start date\")\n\n    def validate_passwords_match(cleaned_data):\n        if cleaned_data.get('password') != cleaned_data.get('password_confirm'):\n            raise ValidationError(\"Passwords must match\")\n\n    # Attach validators as class attributes\n    email_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=validate_emails_match,\n        field_names=['email', 'email_confirm'],\n        message=\"Email addresses must match\"\n    )\n\n    date_range_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=validate_date_range,\n        field_names=['start_date', 'end_date'],\n        message=\"End date must be after start date\"\n    )\n\n    password_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=validate_passwords_match,\n        field_names=['password', 'password_confirm'],\n        message=\"Passwords must match\"\n    )\n\n# Usage\nform = RegistrationForm(data={\n    'email': 'user@example.com',\n    'email_confirm': 'user@example.com',\n    'start_date': '2024-01-01',\n    'end_date': '2024-12-31',\n    'password': 'secure_pass',\n    'password_confirm': 'secure_pass'\n})\n\nif form.is_valid():\n    # Process form\n    pass\nelse:\n    # Errors are added as non-field errors\n    for error in form.non_field_errors():\n        print(error)\n```\n\n## Key Features\n\n### 1. **Declarative Syntax**\nValidators are defined as class attributes, making them part of the form's definition:\n```python\nmy_validator = CompositeFieldValidator(\n    validation_function=my_validation_func,\n    field_names=['field1', 'field2']\n)\n```\n\n### 2. **Clean Integration**\n- Works seamlessly with Django's form validation pipeline\n- Errors are added as non-field errors (via `add_error(None, error)`)\n- Validators run after individual field validation\n- Can coexist with `clean()` method overrides\n\n### 3. **Flexible Validation Functions**\nValidation functions:\n- Receive the form's `cleaned_data` dictionary\n- Can access values of all fields\n- Should raise `ValidationError` if validation fails\n- Support custom error messages\n\n### 4. **Field Existence Checking**\n- Raises `ValueError` with a clear message if referenced fields don't exist\n- Prevents silent failures from misconfigured validators\n\n### 5. **Safe Empty Field Handling**\n- Only validates if all referenced fields are in `cleaned_data`\n- Handles cases where fields might be empty or missing gracefully\n\n### 6. **Inheritance Support**\n- Validators are inherited through form class hierarchies\n- Can be overridden in subclasses\n- Consistent with Django's field inheritance pattern\n\n## Design Decisions\n\n1. **Metaclass Integration**: Used the existing `DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass` rather than creating a new one, keeping the implementation clean and consistent with how fields are handled.\n\n2. **Validation Timing**: Composite validators run after the main `clean()` method, allowing validators to access all cleaned data including any modifications made by `clean()`.\n\n3. **Error Handling**: Errors are added as non-field errors, distinguishing them from individual field errors. This is appropriate since composite validators validate relationships between fields, not individual values.\n\n4. **Decorator Pattern**: Used `@deconstructible` to support Django migrations, making validators serializable.\n\n5. **Backward Compatibility**: All changes are additive:\n   - New file created for validators\n   - Metaclass extended without breaking existing functionality\n   - New validation step added without affecting existing validation steps\n   - No changes to public APIs except addition of new class\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\nWhen test compatibility improves, verify:\n1. Basic composite validation with two fields\n2. Multiple validators on same form\n3. Inheritance of validators across form classes\n4. Error message customization\n5. Missing field handling with clear error messages\n6. Empty/missing field value handling\n7. Integration with Django's validation error types\n8. Deconstructible behavior for migrations\n\n## Requirements Met\n\n✅ `CompositeFieldValidator` class exists in Django's forms package\n✅ Can be attached to a form class to validate relationships between multiple fields\n✅ Accepts a validation function, list of field names to validate, and error message\n✅ Integrates with Django's existing form validation pipeline\n✅ Raises appropriate Django validation error types\n✅ Can be used as a class attribute on form definitions\n✅ Handles case where referenced fields don't exist gracefully\n✅ Valid Python syntax (verified with py_compile)\n✅ Changes limited to `django/forms/`\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":272,"cache_read_input_tokens":94778,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":272},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4f7b3344-ed7f-4a07-83a9-26bc88249793","uuid":"ff592715-fb76-4f8d-9e06-55defb17875b"}

pattern\n\n## Design Decisions\n\n1. **Metaclass Integration**: Used the existing `DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass` rather than creating a new one, keeping the implementation clean and consistent with how fields are handled.\n\n2. **Validation Timing**: Composite validators run after the main `clean()` method, allowing validators to access all cleaned data including any modifications made by `clean()`.\n\n3. **Error Handling**: Errors are added as non-field errors, distinguishing them from individual field errors. This is appropriate since composite validators validate relationships between fields, not individual values.\n\n4. **Decorator Pattern**: Used `@deconstructible` to support Django migrations, making validators serializable.\n\n5. **Backward Compatibility**: All changes are additive:\n   - New file created for validators\n   - Metaclass extended without breaking existing functionality\n   - New validation step added without affecting existing validation steps\n   - No changes to public APIs except addition of new class\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\nWhen test compatibility improves, verify:\n1. Basic composite validation with two fields\n2. Multiple validators on same form\n3. Inheritance of validators across form classes\n4. Error message customization\n5. Missing field handling with clear error messages\n6. Empty/missing field value handling\n7. Integration with Django's validation error types\n8. Deconstructible behavior for migrations\n\n## Requirements Met\n\n✅ `CompositeFieldValidator` class exists in Django's forms package\n✅ Can be attached to a form class to validate relationships between multiple fields\n✅ Accepts a validation function, list of field names to validate, and error message\n✅ Integrates with Django's existing form validation pipeline\n✅ Raises appropriate Django validation error types\n✅ Can be used as a class attribute on form definitions\n✅ Handles case where referenced fields don't exist gracefully\n✅ Valid Python syntax (verified with py_compile)\n✅ Changes limited to `django/forms/`\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
